**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# GCC Stack Clash Protection Implementation Audit

## Your Task

Audit the stack clash protection implementation in GCC. Find all C/C++ source files in `gcc-mirror/gcc` that implement stack clash mitigation. Specifically: 1. The file that implements stack clash probing for x86_64 targets (`gcc/config/i386/i386.cc` — look for `stack_clash_protection`). 2. The file that implements the generic stack clash expansion (`gcc/explow.cc` — look for `anti_adjust_stack_and_probe`). 3. The header where `TARGET_STACK_CLASH_PROTECTION` is declared or defined. 4. The test file under `gcc/testsuite/gcc.target/i386/` that validates stack clash protection (look for `stack-clash-*`). 5. The common options file where `-fstack-clash-protection` is defined (`gcc/common.opt`). Report each file path and the key function or definition.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

68-assistanttext-
I've completed a comprehensive audit of the GCC stack clash protection implementation. Here's what I found:

## Summary

The analysis reveals a **well-architected, generic implementation** of stack clash protection that spans across multiple GCC components:

### Key Files Located:

1. **Core Implementation**: `gcc/explow.cc` and `gcc/explow.h` - Generic stack clash functions used across all architectures
2. **x86 Integration**: `gcc/config/i386/i386.cc` - x86_64 backend integration
3. **Command-line Interface**: `gcc/common.opt` and `gcc/params.opt` - Flag and parameter definitions
4. **Target Hook System**: `gcc/target.def`, `gcc/targhooks.cc`, `gcc/targhooks.h` - Architecture customization points
5. **Validation**: `gcc/toplev.cc` - Compilation-time validation
6. **Test Suite**: Multiple test files in `gcc/testsuite/gcc.target/i386/` including:
   - `stack-clash-protection.c` (primary test)
   - `stack-check-11.c` through `stack-check-19.c` (regression tests)
   - PR test files (pr84128.c, pr83994.c, pr84064.c)

### Key Symbols:

The implementation centers around 5 main functions in `gcc/explow.cc`:
- `anti_adjust_stack_and_probe_stack_clash()` - Main protection routine
- `compute_stack_clash_protection_loop_data()` - Probe calculation
- `emit_stack_clash_protection_probe_loop_start()` - Loop initialization
- `emit_stack_clash_protection_probe_loop_end()` - Loop completion
- `anti_adjust_stack_and_probe()` - Generic probing

### Design Highlights:

- **Generic implementation** reused by x86, ARM64, PowerPC, RISC-V, LoongArch, and S390
- **Target customization** via `TARGET_STACK_CLASH_PROTECTION_ALLOCA_PROBE_RANGE` hook
- **Parameterizable protection** with guard size and probe interval controls
- **Smart loop generation** that unrolls small allocations inline

Two related parameters control the behavior: stack-clash-protection-guard-size (gcc/params.opt:1108-1110) and stack-clash-protection-probe-interval (gcc/params.opt:1112-1114), both representing powers of 2 for guard and probe distances.\\n\\n2. **Compilation and Validation (gcc/toplev.cc)**: At lines 1650-1656, the compiler validates that stack clash protection is not used on targets where the stack grows upward (which would make the protection ineffective). The -fstack-clash-protection flag is rejected for such targets.\\n\\n3. **Target Hook Interface (gcc/target.def, gcc/targhooks.*)**: The mechanism provides a target hook TARGET_STACK_CLASH_PROTECTION_ALLOCA_PROBE_RANGE (gcc/target.def:6534-6545) allowing architectures to define ABI-specific probe ranges. The default implementation in gcc/targhooks.cc:2744+ (default_stack_clash_protection_alloca_probe_range) returns 0, allowing generic behavior. Function prototypes are declared in gcc/targhooks.h:305.\\n\\n4. **Generic Implementation (gcc/explow.cc, gcc/explow.h)**: The core stack clash protection logic resides in gcc/explow.cc:\\n\\n   a. **allocate_dynamic_stack_space (gcc/explow.cc:1443+)**: High-level function that allocates dynamic stack space. When flag_stack_clash_protection is set, it calls anti_adjust_stack_and_probe_stack_clash instead of the standard anti_adjust_stack_and_probe (lines 1645-1646).\\n\\n   b. **anti_adjust_stack_and_probe_stack_clash (gcc/explow.cc:2072-2142)**: Implements the stack clash protection mechanism for dynamic allocations. This function:\\n      - Ensures the size is in Pmode (line 2075-2076)\\n      - Calls compute_stack_clash_protection_loop_data to calculate probe parameters (line 2082-2083)\\n      - Retrieves target-specific probe range via targetm.stack_clash_protection_alloca_probe_range() (line 2086)\\n      - For small allocations (\u22644*probe_interval), emits inline probes (line 2098-2108)\\n      - For larger allocations, emits a probing loop using emit_stack_clash_protection_probe_loop_start/end\\n\\n   c. **compute_stack_clash_protection_loop_data (gcc/explow.cc:1955-2004)**: Calculates loop parameters:\\n      - Extracts probe_interval from param_stack_clash_protection_probe_interval (line 1961-1962)\\n      - Rounds the allocation size down to probe_interval boundary (line 1963-1964)\\n      - Computes the final stack pointer value (last_addr) (line 1969-1972)\\n      - Calculates residual bytes not covered by the loop (line 1976)\\n\\n   d. **emit_stack_clash_protection_probe_loop_start (gcc/explow.cc:2014+)**: Emits RTL instructions for loop initialization, including loop label and initial comparison.\\n\\n   e. **emit_stack_clash_protection_probe_loop_end (gcc/explow.cc:2036+)**: Emits RTL instructions for the loop body and termination logic.\\n\\n5. **x86_64 Integration (gcc/config/i386/i386.cc)**: While the generic mechanism in gcc/explow.cc handles most of the work, gcc/config/i386/i386.cc provides x86-specific prologue/epilogue generation and frame management. The x86 backend leverages the generic stack clash protection functions defined in gcc/explow.cc.\\n\\n6. **Function Declarations (gcc/explow.h:70-87)**: All stack clash protection functions are declared as:\\n   - anti_adjust_stack_and_probe_stack_clash(rtx) (line 78)\\n   - compute_stack_clash_protection_loop_data(...) This implementation prevents this by:\\n1. Probing at regular intervals (typically 4KB on x86)\\n2. Never skipping probes even for small allocations\\n3. Using mandatory probes for all dynamic allocations when -fstack-clash-protection is enabled\\n4. Respecting the OS guard page size (typically 4KB on Linux)\"\n}\n",
